Shanghai and Hong Kong Harbors Filled with Foreign Warships; Eleven Steamships Also Entering and Leaving 119

The Zi Lin News reports that a squadron of British submarines, making their annual summer cruise to the north, will soon arrive in Shanghai. This is the first time in several years. Another similar number of American submarines will arrive at almost the same time, and cruisers and destroyers from Britain, the United States, and Japan will also converge, making Shanghai resemble a naval base. The British submarine squadron, along with the supply ship HMS Medway, is expected to enter the harbor from Hong Kong on Friday and will remain until May 12, before sailing to Weihaiwei. These warships are not commonly seen in Shanghai, as they have been based between Hong Kong and Weihaiwei for several years and have not passed through Shanghai. The American submarines, on the other hand, have passed through Shanghai twice in one year. The last time they arrived in Shanghai was at the end of October last year, sailing from Qingdao to Manila to participate in the Philippine inauguration ceremony. And during the annual naval exercises, the American submarine squadron will also follow the supply ship USS Canopus. Last Friday, eight American destroyers arrived in Shanghai from Manila. This is the vanguard of the American fleet stationed in Asia. Fourteen more ships are expected to arrive from the south this week, followed by six more. On Thursday, the flagship of the American fleet, USS Waco, will return to Shanghai from Beijing. The American transport ship USS Chaumont will also enter the port. Other warships docked in the Huangpu River include two Japanese training cruisers and the flagship of the Japanese Third Fleet. In addition, there is also a French warship. According to unconfirmed reports, the British cruiser HMS Kent may arrive in Shanghai next Thursday. It is estimated that by the end of next week, there will be about forty warships docked in Shanghai Harbor, a rare sight in this city.

From today (the 18th) to the next four days, the arrival and departure of steamships in Shanghai Harbor will also be at an unprecedented peak, with a total of eleven ships with a total gross tonnage of over 187,000 tons. The largest of these is the Empress of Russia, with a gross tonnage of 26,032 tons, which is expected to arrive from Canada on Tuesday, carrying a large number of spring tourists. Another Japanese steamship is also expected to arrive on the same day. A total of three ships are expected to arrive today, and five are expected to arrive tomorrow. The exact number of passengers and cargo unloaded in Shanghai by each ship is not yet known, but the number is certain to be large, as many of the ships are fully loaded with passengers.

Weather Report 120

The Shanghai Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that the Bohai Sea is clear with sandstorms and strong west to northwest winds. The Yangtze River basin and this area have moderate south to west winds. The East China Sea will change from overcast to clear with south to southwest winds. Also, within the 24 hours prior to 3:00 p.m. yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 71.2 degrees and the lowest was 47.3 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 66.7 degrees and the lowest was 43.0 degrees.

Acknowledgment: Thank you to Mr. Huang Jianzhong of the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Publishing House for the gift of "Latest Detailed Map of the South Sea Islands" yesterday.

Closing of the Architectural Exhibition - Announcement of Important Declaration Stating Five Points 121

The Chinese Architectural Exhibition, which has been open to the public for eight days at the City Center Museum and the new building of the Chinese Aviation Association, concluded yesterday, which also happened to be a holiday. Throughout the day, over a thousand people visited, making it extremely crowded. Even around 5 PM, hundreds of people were still requesting to enter, with some coming from as far as Suzhou. Therefore, the museum extended its closing time by one hour. In total, the exhibition saw 45,000 visitors over its eight-day run, including students from more than 110 elementary schools. This level of activity in the city center area had not been seen since the National Games.

In other news, at 5 PM yesterday, the association held a meeting for initiators at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA. Attendees included Ye Gongchuo, Huang Boqiao, Zhou Ren, Shen Yi, Li Qianruo, Zhuang Jun, Du Yengeng, Wu Derun, Lu Shusen, Chen Duanzhi, Zhang Xiaoliang, Li Dachao, Hu Zhaochun, Sun Menggang, Wang Xingyuan, and over thirty others. Ye Gongchuo, as the chairman, conducted the meeting with due formality. First, the chairman reported on the exhibition's progress, income, and expenses. Then, the following resolutions were discussed and passed: the association's declaration proposal (passed); the association's draft submission to the Executive Yuan (passed); the proposal to publish a commemorative volume (passed), and Ye Gongchuo, Liang Sicheng, Dong Dayou, Du Yengeng, Xu Weinan, Hu Zhaochun, and Chen Duanzhi were elected as editorial committee members; the proposal on how to make up for the association's significant financial shortfall (passed), and Zhang Xiaoliang, Li Dachao, Lu Fengzhang, Tang Jingxian, and Dong Dayou were tasked with raising the necessary funds; the proposal to ensure the association's permanent existence (passed), and Ye Gongchuo, Shen Yi, Zhu Qiqian, Zhang Xiaoliang, Li Dachao, Guan Songsheng, Zhuang Jun, Du Yengeng, and Dong Daxi were elected to design a plan. The proposal to express gratitude on behalf of the assembly to the association's president Ye and all staff members, and to send letters of appreciation to exhibitors (passed), and the administrative department was tasked with handling it. The original text of the association's declaration is recorded below:

Housing is one of the four major issues of people's livelihood. In recent years, as our country strives for construction, its importance has become increasingly prominent. However, since the introduction of Western architecture, our country's inherent architecture has undergone significant changes. Choosing the best and discarding the worst has yet to yield a final conclusion. As a result, architectural styles often progress along irregular paths, becoming more and more diverse but also increasingly chaotic. It is extremely rare to find originality and unique design expression. As for building materials, they are imported from foreign countries in an endless stream, costing the country at least tens of millions of dollars annually. Its impact on people's livelihood is undoubtedly severe. Feeling deeply about this, we initiated the Chinese Architectural Exhibition, seeking over two thousand items in five major categories: models, drawings, materials, tools, and publications. These were displayed publicly at the Shanghai Museum and the Shanghai Chinese Aviation Association. Additionally, we invited celebrities and experts to deliver speeches at the Shanghai YMCA on important architectural issues, hoping to raise public awareness and discussion. From April 12th to 19th, the exhibition lasted eight days, with thousands of visitors each day, proving that construction issues have indeed drawn deep attention from the public. Based on the purpose of the meeting and the results of recent exchanges of views, this association deeply believes that if the current state of China's architectural community is not urgently changed, time will easily pass, and money, which is hard to come by, will be wasted in vain. Failure to create an authentic architectural style would be the greatest crisis for our national culture. However, it is not too late to address this now, and real reform requires action, not just words. Therefore, we specifically highlight the most fundamental points, which colleagues unanimously believe require societal attention and government advocacy, as stated below. We hope that our fellow countrymen will give it their consideration. Education on architecture should be urgently emphasized in all schools. In modern times, scientific progress and technological advancement rely on specialized education as their foundation. Architecture is no exception. In recent years, due to various new constructions in the country, tens of millions of dollars are spent annually. The number of architects and supervisors needed in construction is estimated to be over several thousand, while the number of such talents trained domestically is no more than a hundred per year. Among the public and private universities nationwide, only a few, such as the Central University in the capital and the Qinqin University in Guangzhou, have established architecture departments. They are pioneering with limited resources, and their facilities are largely incomplete. There are even fewer institutions dedicated to training mid-level specialized personnel. The mismatch between supply and demand is so significant that it is no wonder the performance of architecture is poor, thereby affecting the overall performance of construction. Therefore, we earnestly request the Executive Yuan to instruct the central and local education authorities to promote architectural education, expand training facilities, or establish an architectural academy at the central level dedicated to specialized training, so that a larger number of talents can be cultivated to meet the urgent needs of reality. Domestically produced building materials should be vigorously promoted. It is found that of the newer types of building materials used in public and private constructions nationwide, those taken from foreign countries account for more than seven-tenths. The annual outflow is no less than several tens of millions of dollars. Since the establishment of the National Government in the 17th year of the Republic, this must have amounted to hundreds of millions of dollars by now, a staggering sum. If we do not urgently remedy this, we will continue to talk about construction while becoming increasingly impoverished and weak, which is cause for great concern. According to the industries related to construction, such as steelmaking, ironmaking, copper production, afforestation, timber production, paint production, pigments, glass, ceramics, cement, bricks, tiles, stone, and various decorations, are directly and indirectly related to the livelihood of the people and the balance of power. Observing the general psychology, it is known that the outflow of money is alarming, but domestic products are simply insufficient to meet the demand. Sometimes, even when domestic products are usable, poor management and a lack of marketing skills result in them being unavailable. Engineers and the construction industry, fearing difficulties and seeking convenience, develop habits, further blocking the path of domestic product development. The cycle of cause and effect leads to a downward spiral. In times of crisis, the danger would be even more unspeakable. It is requested that the Executive Yuan promptly circulate instructions to all agencies inside and outside the capital, requiring that domestic materials be used as much as possible in all new constructions, and instruct the Ministry of Finance, Industry, and Railways, as well as the provincial and municipal governments, to make every effort to support the above-mentioned industries in design, operation, freight, and taxation, to enable them to emerge, establish, and develop, and to supervise their production volume and quality, so that they are useful and suitable. In this way, benefits can be kept within the country, and utilization can be more self-reliant. Standards and specifications for building materials should be developed promptly. The most urgent specifications to be established for building materials are nothing more than quality and dimensions. Currently, the standards for the quality of building materials on the domestic market either follow the customs of other countries or are self-defined by the businesses, resulting in extremely chaotic standards and diverse names. Dimensional standards are even more lacking in uniformity. Although major cities such as Nanjing, Shanghai, and Beiping have some regulations, they are each governed independently and are not unified. The quality standards, names, and dimensions of building materials are practically non-existent. As a result, the progress of construction projects is often hampered, and the safety of people's lives and property lacks protection. If the government formulates quality standards, verifies names, and unifies dimensions and grades for various building materials such as cement, timber, steel, bricks, tiles, hardware, glass, paint, etc., then the system in all regions will be unified, and inferior goods will find it difficult to be substituted and deceive. Product manufacturers, planners, and owners will all benefit. Furthermore, industrial hazards will be reduced daily due to strict restrictions on quality standards such as load-bearing capacity and tensile strength. It can be asserted. It is requested that the Executive Yuan immediately instruct the Ministries of Interior and Industry to formulate these standards as soon as possible to demonstrate renewal and facilitate application. Ancient and famous buildings within the country should be seriously protected by the government through instructions to provincial and municipal governments. China's architecture has historically possessed unique characteristics in the world. Although times and customs have changed, there are still many aspects that can be modeled after. Examples such as the grottoes of Dunhuang and Yungang, the sculptures of Longmen, and the Sarira Pagoda of Qixia all express the spirit of the nation and embody the crystallization of culture, and are important materials for exploring our national art. In recent years, China has focused on modern construction, paying little attention to famous ancient buildings. Furthermore, the common people lack awareness of their preservation, resulting in much damage. Looking at the West, the ancient Roman arena and the Greek temples, although in ruins, embody the great spirit of their nations. Therefore, the preservation of architectural relics is not only an aid to museums but also serves to promote the virtues of the nation. Furthermore, the current question in Chinese architecture is how to create a new style that does not merely imitate Europe and the West, nor is it limited by tradition, but seeks to adapt to national customs, real life, and economic conditions. Therefore, the advantages of China's inherent architecture urgently need to be studied and referenced. It is requested that the Executive Yuan instruct the Ministries of Interior and Education, the Central Antiquities Preservation Committee, and the provincial and municipal governments to seriously protect famous buildings and their relics from all dynasties, urging officials and civilians to take effective measures and not treat this as a mere formality, so that the future of culture and economy will benefit. All agencies related to architectural duties should uniformly employ architectural experts and provide more job opportunities for architects. Architects are similar to ordinary engineers but are actually different. The key elements of architecture are safety, practicality, and aesthetics. Engineers are only responsible for the structural safety of buildings, while architects are not. Architects must also seek to combine practicality, sturdiness, and beauty. Structural safety is certainly a key point, but as times progress and matters become more complex, it is undoubtedly necessary for buildings to be suitable for their specialized purposes. Considering location and economy, and planning for savings, architecture inherently belongs to art, and its patterns and methods are the means to showcase national culture. Therefore, the services of architects not only meet the needs of enterprises but also allow public works administration to rely on architects to apply their knowledge and experience to guide everything, in order to increase the welfare of the people. Today, public and private buildings are changing rapidly everywhere, but upon further examination, some government offices resemble residences, and some libraries resemble ordinary offices. The three major elements of suitability, sturdiness, and beauty are rarely balanced. Alternatively, there is blind faith in foreign architects, and designs and supervision are sought only from foreigners, without considering whether they are suitable for China's needs or economical. The resulting increase in the use of foreign materials and the suppression of specialized talent are inevitable. Furthermore, the heads of architectural departments in various agencies, due to a lack of talent, often rely on amateurs or those with superficial knowledge to manage public works administration, resulting in inappropriate measures and a lack of supervision and guidance. Therefore, although a huge amount of money is spent on construction each year, specialized domestic talent is not given sufficient opportunity to display their skills, and there is no way to promote the progress and improvement of the architectural industry. It is proposed that the Executive Yuan issue a circular to the entire country, stating that in the future, all positions related to the management of architecture should uniformly employ specialized architectural talent and that non-specialists should no longer be used to fill these positions. Government buildings should provide domestic architects with job opportunities and not readily employ foreign architects, so that they can improve and become versatile talents. This is of no small importance to the development of all new undertakings.

The above five points, approved by the association's general assembly, are considered essential plans that should be promptly submitted to the government for implementation. It is hoped that all colleagues and comrades in the country will unanimously support them to achieve early realization. Social facilities that should be available (such as factories, etc.) are also expected to be actively prepared in advance to complement government facilities in fulfilling the mission of the architectural community. This is hereby declared.

Anti-Smoking Movement 122

— Wu Kaixian

Also to the compatriots of all circles in Shanghai

The anti-smoking movement did not start today. In the first year of Daoguang in the Qing Dynasty, Ruan Yuan, Governor-General of Liangguang, requested a ban on smoking. In the nineteenth year, Lin Zexu investigated affairs at the Haikou port in Guangdong and began to put theory into practice, strictly prohibiting opium and burning all the opium stored by British merchants. However, imperialists willingly started wars to sell opium, and as a result, we failed in the war and the opium ban was relaxed. After the Xinhai Revolution, President Sun Yat-sen took office as president and started anew with the people, repeatedly reiterating the ban and striving to eliminate opium. Unfortunately, after President Sun retired, political power fell into the hands of the Beiyang warlords. Some borrowed the name of banning smoking to collect money, while others forced people to grow opium to support their troops. As a result, the bans were abolished, and opium flooded the country, causing widespread harm that worsened over time. Recalling the anti-smoking movement of the past century, we deeply lament its inconsistency, its stop-and-go nature, and we cannot help but feel heartbroken and filled with hidden anxieties!

After the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, it made banning smoking and rejecting drugs a matter of urgency. Last year, the Central Political Conference, in order to promote the efficiency of the anti-smoking effort, strengthened the anti-smoking agencies, specially appointed Chairman Chiang as the Anti-Smoking Supervisor, promulgated regulations for punishing offenders, and set a deadline for eliminating opium in order to completely eliminate opium within the statutory years. Over the past year, the results have been remarkable, and international opinion has changed. The great task of banning smoking that has not been accomplished for a century will certainly be completed as scheduled under the leadership of the National Government and Supervisor Chiang, which can be predicted. However, there is one thing that we must pay close attention to: within our country's territory, there are still special areas such as foreign concessions in Shanghai, Tianjin, and Hankou. These special areas, restricted by treaties, are beyond the reach of government power, and have historically been distribution centers for selling opium. All those who willingly drink poison and wallow in forgetfulness also gather here. If we want to completely complete the task of banning smoking, we cannot rely solely on political power in these special areas, but must rely on the efforts of social forces. Chairman Chiang has also seen this, and once earnestly told us: "The situation in China is relatively special. If the work of banning smoking relies solely on the efforts of the government, it is indeed not easy to achieve completely, because there are many places (such as the concessions in Shanghai, Hankou, and Tianjin) and many malpractices (such as foreigners selling drugs within China) that the government's power cannot fully reach. Therefore, in many cases, it is more effective to rely on social forces than to rely solely on the government's power to ban smoking." He also said: "Regarding the international aspect, namely the concessions in Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, and other places, where foreigners directly or indirectly manufacture and sell drugs, which is beyond the reach of our government's power, we can only try our best to arouse the sympathy of international public opinion and use social and moral forces to prevent and control it, so that foreigners who sell drugs for profit will also dare not openly engage in criminal behavior." Therefore, those of us who live in Shanghai must deeply understand the government's bitter determination to ban smoking, assist the government, jointly reject drugs, demonstrate the organizational power of society, and create a strong public opinion to eradicate drugs, so that all Chinese and foreigners who sell drugs for profit and willingly drink poison can no longer use the concession areas as their lairs and no longer use international power as their protection. And so that the anti-smoking movement in the concession areas can be in sync with our government's anti-smoking movement. In this way, the great task of completely eliminating opium can be accomplished.

President Sun once said: "The scourge of opium has afflicted China for a hundred years." Addiction pervades both the noble and the base, spreading throughout the country, causing loss of employment and time, wasting wealth and ruining bodies. If this continues, the race will be lost. The harm caused by this is no less than that of foreign enemies." Those returning from the four northeastern provinces also constantly say that "the enemy is turning our northeastern compatriots black, hoping to destroy their race." Alas! If we do not make efforts to ban smoking today, not only will we, as Lin Zexu said, have no money to raise and no soldiers to train, but racial destruction is already imminent. This is what the enemy is praying for. Can we turn a blind eye and stand idly by? There are many ways to save the country, and banning smoking is an essential one. Compatriots of all circles in Shanghai, you also know what to strive for!

Smoking Ban and National Revival 123

— Lu Jingtu

The prosperity or decline of a nation is based on the soundness of each individual that constitutes it. China's national strength has declined drastically over the past century, and it can be said that the main reason for this decline is the harm caused by opium. The Anglo-Chinese War, caused by the opium issue, created the deeply rooted power of imperialism in our country, opened the door to aggression by the great powers, and was the biggest fatal injury to our nation's survival. Domestically, opium seedlings are everywhere, and the farmland in the border provinces is almost entirely planted with poisonous substances, which makes food scarce and forces us to rely on foreign rice. The money lost each year is countless. At the same time, the people are deeply addicted to opium, which not only wastes money and interferes with work, causing individuals to fall into bankruptcy, but also weakens their physical constitution, thus causing the national spirit to decline to an irreversible level. If we allow it to continue, in a hundred years the whole country will probably become a nation of opium addicts and sick people, and we will destroy ourselves without waiting for others to invade. The intensity of this invisible opium disaster is actually much greater than any political, military, or economic aggression.

Therefore, China's current problem is not just how to resist foreign aggression, but also how to completely ban smoking. The history of banning smoking in China is already long. At the end of the Ming Dynasty, the government began to ban smoking, but unfortunately the methods used in the past were not appropriate. Either they were too hasty or they became indulgent. As a result, they were not effective. In addition, since the founding of the Republic of China, there have been years of civil war and warlord separatism, which led to the abandonment of the anti-smoking policy and instead allowed opium to spread throughout the country, becoming more and more intense. This is truly a heartbreaking thing from the standpoint of the nation.

Since the establishment of the National Government, the central government has recognized that the nation will not be able to rise until the opium is completely eliminated. Therefore, it has listed banning smoking as an important policy. Recently, it has formulated a six-year plan to ban smoking. The inland provinces are uniformly prohibited from planting, and the remote provinces are also designated counties to reduce production within a time limit. At the same time, opium addicts are ordered to register and gradually quit within a time limit. Extremely strict laws have been promulgated, imposing the death penalty, life imprisonment, or long-term imprisonment on those who plant, manufacture, transport, sell, or harbor and accept bribes. It is stipulated that opium cases will not be handled by the Common Court, but will be tried and executed by military judicial organs in order to expedite matters. The responsibility for the promotion, supervision, and guidance of the entire plan is personally presided over by Chairman Chiang. This is a completely different approach from the previous anti-smoking policies and is enough to show the government's determination in this regard.

However, the government has formulated such severe laws out of the intention to emphasize the importance of chaos and is also a necessary means. However, laws are dead, and the laws themselves will not take effect. They rely entirely on people to implement them, and it is important for the people to truly awaken and cooperate with the government to earnestly implement the anti-smoking plan. The current anti-smoking authorities have specially allowed opium addicts to register without punishment during the reporting period. This does not mean that there will be any changes or suspensions in the entire anti-smoking plan. This is to give elderly and sick opium addicts who cannot quit immediately a path to reform. It is hoped that people across the country will work together to promote and make the opium addicts understand the government's good intentions, voluntarily give up addiction as soon as possible, resolve to quit bad habits, and become good citizens again.

Finally, it is also hoped that the national social leaders and intellectuals will use the power of public opinion to change the psychology of the people, supplement the shortcomings of government laws, cultivate the people's positive living habits towards the light, and jointly open up a new life for the nation in the future.

Rapid Progress in Agricultural Education - Anhui University's College of Agriculture Contracts to Cultivate 100,000 Acres of Lake Field in Huoqiu to Develop Agricultural Farms - Actively Purchasing Seeding Machines and Establishing an Agricultural Economics Department to Enroll New Students 124

The Anhui Provincial Government, due to the completion of the construction of the floodgates inside and outside the Huai River embankment, urgently needs to cultivate the West Lake fields in Huoqiu that have been drained. In addition to sending personnel to measure and build water conservancy projects, it has also contracted 100,000 acres to Anhui University to serve as the agricultural farm of the university's College of Agriculture. All matters related to the West Lake's project, including the reclamation and leasing of wasteland, the investigation of concealed reclamation and tax increases, and the clearing of wasteland loans, have also been handed over to the personnel dispatched by Anhui University for guidance and handling. Currently, Anhui University has dispatched Feng Zigang, director of the Agronomy Department of the university, leading more than a dozen staff members of the College of Agriculture, carrying more than 80 varieties of rice seeds entrusted to the university for testing by the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute, to plant them for trial. They have also requested the provincial government to borrow 20,000 yuan from the bank to purchase high-quality rice seeds along the way for planting. The president of the university, Li Shunqing, also took a steamer to Beijing on the 17th to pay a visit to the Minister of Education to discuss the opening of the Agricultural Economics Department and the enrollment of new students in the university's College of Agriculture next year. It is reported that the original plan of the university's College of Agriculture was to establish the Agronomy Department in the first year, the Agricultural Economics Department in the second year (25th year of the Republic), and the Forestry Department in the third year (26th year of the Republic) to meet the needs of Anhui Province. It is heard that President Li will proceed to Suzhou and Shanghai after completing his official business in Beijing to purchase machines and agricultural tools for sowing, deciding, planting, cultivating, and harvesting, so that they can be transported to Huoqiu for large-scale cultivation.

Elementary School Student Calligraphy Finals: Chong Ding Xiangyuan Wins Championship; Second, Bo Huaying; Third, Shen Yuanxing; Chairman Huang Zaoxiong Gives Speech and Awards 129

The Shanghai Education Association hosted the citywide elementary school student calligraphy competition. Representatives selected from preliminary rounds in each district held the finals yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM in the auditorium of Junyi Middle School on Jumen Road in the Nanshi district. Executive director of the association, Huang Zaoxiong, judges Tong Xingbai, Ma Gongyu, and Li Xiaobai, along with over fifty contestants from various districts, were present.

Chairman's Address: Chairman Huang Zaoxiong first delivered a speech, stating, "Ever since the abolition of the imperial examination and the rise of schools, students generally have rarely studied or paid attention to calligraphy. Although elementary and middle schools have calligraphy courses, they only briefly demonstrate strokes and talk about structure in a very superficial way. Therefore, modern students, even after graduating from university, still do not know what calligraphy is. Truly excellent calligraphers are rare. It should be known that calligraphy is one of the Six Arts, and is also recognized as an art form today. The Shanghai Education Association is therefore holding this elementary school student calligraphy competition to arouse a considerable understanding and interest in calligraphy among elementary school students throughout the city, encouraging them to study diligently. We also hope that elementary school student calligraphy competitions will be held in all provinces, cities, counties, townships, and villages across the country to revive calligraphy. Hopefully, this can be expected. I hope all the young friends will work harder, strive forward, and advance."

List of Winners: After the speech, the competition began. Each person wrote one sheet each of large and small script. The large script used the seven characters "Peace, Struggle, Save China," and the small script used Sun Yat-sen's Last Will and Testament. The allotted time was one hour. The judging results were: First, Ding Xiangyuan (Chongzheng); Second, Bo Huaying (Yongxing); Third, Shen Yuanxing (Gan Gong); Fourth, Wu Lizhi (Dunhua), Zhang Fengxiang (Fudan), Cai Ruiyao (Jinghua); Fifth, Wang Qichang (Shanghai); Sixth, Lu (Xicheng); Seventh, Guo Shurong (Shanghai), Zhang Zhongliang (Qiuzhi), Gao Chunhong (Wusong), Liu Yingda (Sanyu); Eighth, Zhao Boyun (Chengzhong); Ninth, Cai Shanghe (Ningbo No. 2 Elementary School); Tenth, Li Yiding (Jingye Affiliated Elementary School), Zhou Wensheng (Shuji). After the competition, the judges gave guidance, and then Huang Zaoxiong presented the awards.

City Elementary Education Research Association: District Research Begins Today; Research Center Topics Designated by the Education Bureau; Dates and Locations of District Meetings Also Determined 132

The topics for the research centers of the district elementary education research association have been designated separately by the Education Bureau. It is now decided that each district will begin district research starting today. The dates and locations have also been determined. All school principals and teaching affairs directors or research directors of multi-grade schools must attend on time. The meeting dates, locations, and important matters are listed below:

Dates and Locations: Hunei District 1: April 20, 1:00 PM, Yangzheng Elementary School; Hunei District 2: April 20, 4:00 PM, Wanzhu Elementary School; Zhabei District: April 21, 1:00 PM, Qimei Elementary School; Special District 1: April 21, 4:00 PM, He'an Elementary School; Special District 2: April 22, 1:00 PM, Bide Elementary School; Zhenru District: April 22, 4:00 PM, Zhenru Elementary School; City Center District: April 23, 1:00 PM, Center Experimental Elementary School; Jiangwan District: April 23, 4:00 PM, Qiujiang Elementary School; Yangjing District: April 24, 1:00 PM, Zhenxiu Elementary School; Tangqiao District: April 24, 4:00 PM, Tangpan Elementary School; Caojing District: April 25, 1:00 PM, Qiuzhi Elementary School; Wusong District: April 26, 9:00 AM, Wusong Elementary School; Gaoqiao District: April 26, 1:00 PM, Gaoqiao Elementary School; Yinxiang District: April 27, 4:00 PM, Yinxi Elementary School; Pengpu District: April 28, 4:00 PM, Pengpu Elementary School; Yinhang District: April 29, 4:00 PM, Yinhang Elementary School; Gaohang District: April 30, 4:00 PM, Donggou Elementary School; Luhang District: May 1, 4:00 PM, Sanxiu Experimental Elementary School; Yangsi District: May 2, 4:00 PM, Yangsi Elementary School; Pusong District 1: May 3, 9:00 AM, Shicun Elementary School; Pusong District 2: May 2, 1:00 PM, Yangcao Elementary School; Fahua District: May 4, 1:00 PM, Honglu Elementary School.

Important Matters: The attendees for the tenth meeting of each district this year should be the principals of each school and the teaching affairs directors or research directors of multi-grade schools. With the exception of single-grade elementary schools with one person per school, which may suspend classes for a few hours as needed during non-holidays or after-school meeting times, all others must arrange substitute teachers and are not allowed to suspend classes for vacation. Schools in each district should still follow the districts designated in the previous session. The important work of this meeting is to meticulously formulate research outlines and details in accordance with the designated research centers, and to distribute research work according to the formulated research outlines and details. Each school should prepare a draft of the above research outline and details before the meeting as a basis for proposal discussion, so as to achieve full preparation. After the research work is distributed according to the research outline and details, each school principal should immediately submit it to the school affairs meeting for joint discussion and implementation, so as to achieve the effect of universal research and collective wisdom. The research outline and details and the research work distribution method should be submitted by each chairman to the bureau for approval within one week after the meeting. Questions outside the prescribed research center can also be raised for discussion or research, but should be reported in detail by each chairman after the meeting. The date of the second meeting should be six weeks after the first meeting. Each association should specify the time for each school to submit research reports to the association and strictly follow it. The chairman of each association should separately notify each school of the important matters of the first decision-making meeting to facilitate preparation.

First 30,000-Meter Relay Race: Yibing Jia Wins Championship; Time: 1 Hour, 25 Minutes, 3 Seconds, 4 Tenths; Runner-Up Hongkou Jia Also Strong 137

The first 30,000-meter long-distance relay race (divided into four stages, the first stage is 5,000 meters, the second stage is 7,480 meters, the third stage is 4,228 meters, and the last stage is 4,920 meters, totaling 21,628 meters) organized by the Jingwu Athletic Association started at 10:30 AM yesterday at the west side gate of Hongkou Park. There were originally eleven teams participating, but Yibing Yi and Zhonghua Yi were absent due to temporary absences, so only nine teams actually competed. As a result, Yibing Jia had particularly complete talents and won the championship with a time of one hour, twenty-five minutes, three seconds, and five tenths. The runner-up was Hongkou Jia. The details of yesterday's race are recorded below:

Gu Qimin: Takes the Lead

At exactly 10:00 AM, the team members gathered inside the west side gate of Hongkou Park. After roll call, the second, third, and fourth runners were sent to their respective destinations by special vehicles from the Jingwu Association. At 10:30 AM, the first runners, under the gunshot of the starter Sun Huipai, moved their hairy legs. Jingwu veteran Xu Yanbo took the lead, but when he reached the intersection of Xiangyin Road, Xu Yanbo went the wrong way. When he realized it and returned, he had already gone 80 meters in the wrong direction, and was surpassed by Gu Qimin of the Yan She. The first 5,000-meter stage was completed in 19 minutes and 35 seconds.

Ling Xuewen: Sprints with All His Might

In the second stage, Yang Linfa of the Yan She took the baton and ran swiftly. After 50 meters, Ling Xuewen of Yibing Jia and Zhou Ruquan of Jingwu followed closely. Chen Zhiming of Hongkou Jia was 20 meters behind. Yang Linfa suddenly showed that his strength was slightly inferior, and before reaching Jungong Road, he was overtaken by Ling and Zhou. After passing the power plant, Ling Xuewen sprinted with all his might, surpassing Zhou Ruquan by 200 meters. At this time, Ma Riji of Zhonghua Jia showed his skills and surpassed Yang Linfa, Qian Zenglong, and Chen Zhiming from behind, and was not much different from Zhou Ruquan. At the end of the second stage, Ling Xuewen arrived first, followed by Zhou Ruquan and Ma Riji, taking 26 minutes and 12 seconds.

Little Zhang Liang: Runs Ahead

In the third stage, Zhang Liang of Yibing Jia took the baton and ran like a horse freed from its saddle, with light steps and beautiful posture along the way. Wan Jinsheng of Hongkou Jia had ample strength and, silently and without color, had moved from fifth place to second, surpassing Chen Xuzhou, Le Kangyi, and Xi Rurong. The others had no significant changes. When Zhang Liang reached the fourth stage, he left Wan Jinsheng about 500 to 600 meters behind, taking 18 minutes and 22 seconds.

Yibing Jia Wins the Championship

In the fourth stage, the championship was almost certain to go to Yibing Jia. After Wu Wenlin took the baton, he walked forward with a calm posture. Wang Rulin of Hongkou Jia tried his best to chase, but Chen Luzhou of Jingwu gradually felt unsustainable due to lack of strength in the middle. When Gu Huiyuan took over and caught up, there was a difference of 800 meters. Zhu Wenzhang of Zhonghua and Gu advanced shoulder to shoulder, and the first to reach the finish line was Wu Wenlin of Yibing Jia, with a time of 21 minutes, 63 seconds, and five tenths. Wang Rulin of Hongkou Jia fell behind by 500 meters and surrendered to second place. 150 meters behind was Wang Zhenglin of Yibing Bing. Zhu Wenzhang of Zhonghua relied on the final sprint to surpass Gu Huiyuan and reach the finish line first.

Jingwu Association Rewards Merit

After the race, the Jingwu Athletic Association prepared exquisite prizes to encourage the interest of the participating teams. The team champion, Yibing Jia, received a large silver cup, the runner-up, Hongkou Jia, the third place, Yibing Bing, and the fourth place, Zhonghua Jia, each received a silver shield. The association also awarded each of the four players of the team champion, Yibing Jia, namely Guan Youwen, Ling Xuewen, Zhang Liang, and Wu Wenlin, a small silver shield. Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 150

— (Pu)

Society is constantly at war, always at war. This war, however, replaces weapons with intelligence. The result of the war is, of course, that people with high intelligence triumph, and people with poor intelligence fail. The impact of this is no less than that of a war with weapons. However, if people with poor intelligence hold the mentality that "the wise man may make a mistake in a thousand plans, and the foolish man may gain something in a thousand plans," and strive forward, it will not be difficult for them to have their day.

The process of opium smokers, from the initial intake to their death, can be described in detail with five characters "引 (yǐn), 影 (yǐng), 隱 (yǐn), 癮 (yǐn), 尹 (yǐn)" (meaning lead, shadow, conceal, addiction, tomb). Initially, they are "led" by relatives and friends to try it slightly. Soon, they are "shadowed" by its effects on their physiology. When others become suspicious and inquire, they still "conceal" it in every way, without any intention of quitting. Over time, they become "addicted," and from then on, they become weak and frail, with all kinds of diseases. As a result, they "reside" in the tomb. (Note: "尹" is a combination of "一尸," which means the corpse is carried by a wooden pole, meaning death.) Smokers who see this and are still unrepentant are not far from death even if they are not already dead.

After Qingming 151

— Wei Jing

Although very early, in the early spring, women had already put on thin single-layer clothing, experiencing summer attire in the spring. However, that was still limited to a minority. Only after Qingming can it be uniform, with slender jade arms emerging one after another from short sleeves. At the same time, the jade legs also removed wool socks and applied powder. Open-toed high heels, coupled with nail polish surpassing the color of the countryside, seemed to be offering smiles to people.

Obviously, for sock factory owners, after Qingming, it is no less than enduring the most difficult non-golden age of the year. Because after Qingming, everyone has to open their mouths wide and smile desperately at the hard-working masses in the upper class. This is because after Qingming, the leaves on the willow branches all feel stuffy hiding inside and stick out to breathe. In that case, the cotton-padded jackets on the hard-working masses can also be easily taken off, replaced with lined or single-layer clothes, without shivering anymore.

Indeed, after Qingming, the weather is warmer. The Guanyin Festival, the Yuandi Festival, the birthday of the Great Emperor Zhang, and the old monk crossing the river, those dreadful festival reports, have all passed. The spring breeze turns lightly on the earth, promoting the growth of green grass in every corner of the earth. In the city, the pointed shoes of gentlemen and the high heels of women, harmoniously smile at the cattle and sheep gnawing grass in the fields, appearing shy and timid like the girls in the countryside.

No need to be timid, this is precisely the golden age for cattle and sheep, to graze on the green grass as much as possible. After Qingming, before long, the sun will gradually release its scorching heat, gradually urging the farmers to pant and sweat. Listen, the cuckoo is already calling diligently. Calling, calling, calling people to sow grains, otherwise, oh, if you don’t work, don’t complain about your stomach being upset with hunger.

Crying for Yanshi 152

— Gao Shu'an

Electrical expert Mr. Li Yanshi passed away on March 9th. Time passes quickly, and forty days have already passed in a hurry. In these forty days, I seem to have lost something, feeling confused all day long. He was my close friend, and now he is dead. But I don’t know if it’s sadness? Is it sentimentality? Or is it regret? He was only forty-four years old when he passed away, so his friends from afar sent letters inquiring about the cause of his death.

Yanshi fell ill on December 15th of last year. Initially, he suffered from dizziness and blurred vision, followed by increased blood pressure. Western doctors Jin Wenqi, Zang Boyong, and a certain Japanese doctor were consulted for treatment, and both acupuncture and medication were used. However, the illness continued to worsen... (omission)

Human World Within Reach 153

—

Cooking the Son to Cure Hunger

The diagnosis of Western medicine was as such, so it was decided to consult a Chinese medicine practitioner. On February 18th, he moved out of Baolong Hospital and returned to his residence for treatment. He took the prescriptions of Chinese medicine practitioners Zhang Yicheng, Wang Zhongqi, Xia Yingtang, and Ying Fufang. In the middle, the condition fluctuated and changed constantly. Yanshi usually had great faith in Western doctor Shen Linbo, especially as a childhood friend. Seeing this situation, he urgently telegraphed Dr. Shen Linbo in Beiping. He arrived at the residence on March 1st for treatment. Yanshi held my hand and said, "Linbo has arrived, and my illness can be entrusted to him." He also inquired about the situation of my daughter Zhifang in medical school, and said that Du He Jianhou Zhi Sun also sent letters to inquire about his condition, asking me to thank them for their kindness. However, the conclusion of Dr. Linbo's examination on this day was the same as that of other doctors, believing that the condition was extremely dangerous and could not be saved. However, his face was already swollen, and his eyes were almost blind. The condition was extremely urgent. On the evening of the 9th, I suddenly received a phone call saying that Yanshi had passed away. The body had been placed in a coffin at the Shanghai Funeral Home. Alas! Who would have expected that that meeting would become a final farewell? That night, I was extremely sad, tossing and turning, unable to sleep. The next day, I sent Yanshi's portrait to the newspaper office. When I talked to Jianhou about Yanshi's sincerity in treating others, I couldn't help but cry. (Omission below)

In terms of Yanshi's age, he was in his prime, handsome and formidable. He should not have died. Furthermore, with the rapid progress of China's construction now, a large number of talents are needed, and especially the current leaders, who can possess the spirit of both scholarship and courage like Mr. Yanshi, creating many careers in a short period of time and achieving great success. I am afraid that they are rare and difficult to find. And Yanshi should not have died even more today, when powerful neighbors are pressing in and the country is in serious trouble. But now Yanshi has finally died. What is the impact on society, when the coffin is closed and the final judgment is made? Not only has the electrical industry promoted a leader, but with his spirit of diligent service and meticulous work, it can also be said that we have lost a mentor. Therefore, after Yanshi's death, he earned the bitter tears of many people, and there were reasons for all of them. Now, when various groups and colleagues in the electrical industry, as well as friends from his lifetime, held a memorial meeting at the Lake Society yesterday, there were many more solemn eulogies. Alas, Yanshi! You have now shed your skin and flown away, but when I think of the past, there is only sadness, only sentimentality, no, it is also regret! (Returned thanks)

Life in Spring 155

— Feng Moni

Because the spring is still cold, I feel the climate is too cool. In my attic room, the cold is even more severe. Without proper clothing, it is really difficult to bear, especially since the floor is cement, making it feel even more gloomy. So, I thought of a solution, discussing it with the second landlord to move to the newly built three-story loft.

Although I have to bend over to walk into the three-story loft, and I often bump my head, I am very dissatisfied in my heart. However, compared to the attic room, it is much warmer, and the rent is cheaper, so I reluctantly settled down.

But the climate suddenly became warm, and the three-story loft was not ventilated at all, making it really stuffy. Moreover, the bedbugs lurking in the walls were already stirring, making it impossible to sleep peacefully all night. I felt uncomfortable, so I thought of moving back to the attic room.

Fortunately, the attic room had no tenants. I estimated that my entire property in my pocket was only four French francs. Fortunately, I still had two dollars of manuscript fees to pool together, so I moved back to the attic room. I felt comfortable, and my chest was open and happy, as if I had seen the light again.

Because I am always sitting in the room, I don't know what it is like outside. But when I saw the sister-in-law in the back building wearing an extremely thin silk shirt, I became a little suspicious again. Although the climate is a little warmer, summer clothes are not very suitable after all. So, I went outside to see the spring scenery and, by the way, send two manuscripts.

Walking on the road, I already felt dizzy. Those modern women were all wearing sleeveless long dresses, which was indeed very relaxed. Suddenly, I felt heavy. I was so confused that I didn't even feel hot wearing my broken thick cotton robe. I looked at myself, feeling a little ashamed. I didn't dare to look at others, hanging my head and running in the sunlight. Beads of sweat dripped from my forehead, making everything seem blurry, as if I didn't exist in this world.

Bank Research 159

— Jiansheng
