Economic Publication

The Income Tax Problem 174

— Sen Yu

Recently, the income tax issue has been widely discussed. Since legislator Ma Shichu repeatedly advocated that fiscal policy should first implement income tax during this extraordinary period, this issue has attracted much attention from all parties. It is also heard that the Central Finance Committee and the Economic Committee have scheduled a meeting within days to discuss the issue, and concrete measures are expected to emerge soon.

What exactly is income tax?

So, what exactly is income tax? Let's give a brief overview:

Income tax is a tax directly levied by the state on the economic net income (income) of individuals or legal entities within a certain period. It is a personal tax, and its general advantages are: Wide tax coverage, unlike other taxes such as land tax, house tax, and business tax, which are mostly limited to local areas. Fair burden, regardless of whether it is a direct tax or an indirect tax, all proportional tax systems place a heavy burden on the poor and a light burden on the rich, completely ignoring the ability of citizens to pay taxes. Income tax clearly has its characteristics. One is to distinguish the amount of income, which is called "progressive taxation." The higher the income, the higher the tax rate, so the burden on the wealthy class is heavier. This is even more pronounced on excess income tax. The so-called excess income tax refers to an additional tax with a high progressive rate levied on total income from all sources that exceeds a certain amount, in addition to the ordinary income tax. It is also called additional income tax. The second is to distinguish the nature of income, which is called "differentiation." The most important is to reduce the tax rate on earned income and increase the tax rate on property income, so that the burden on those who gain without labor is increased. Stable income: reliable income is generated during each fixed period. Flexible, most taxes are not easy to change at any time, so the government's policy cannot be implemented when necessary. However, income tax has considerable flexibility. Tax rates can be lowered during peacetime, and it is also easier to change tax rates when necessary, such as during wartime. Tax rates can be increased separately based on the ability of taxpayers at all levels, making it easier for the government to raise emergency funds.

Types of Income Tax and Taxation Methods

Income tax can be divided into the following two categories due to the different standards and scope of collection methods:

Comprehensive Income Tax Comprehensive income tax, also known as general income tax or total income tax, does not consider the source of income, but combines the income of individuals or legal entities from all sources and taxes it based on the total amount. This is the so-called comprehensive taxation system. Its advantage is that progressive rates are easy to achieve and the burden is particularly fair. However, its disadvantage is that it is not easy to conduct investigations and comprehensive work satisfactorily, which often leads to many malpractices. Therefore, without a sound administrative system, it will have unfair tendencies.

Source Income Tax Source income tax, also known as partial or individual income tax, classifies all income according to its categories. Some still require the use of investigation and estimation methods, but some can be deducted in advance from the payer. The advantage is that countries that cannot tax all income at the same time can gradually adopt it, so as not to be too hasty. However, classifying by category may increase collection procedures and costs, and because the effectiveness of progressive rates is reduced, the burden may not always be completely fair.

The above classifies income tax based on the overall scope of taxation methods. Now, we briefly describe various different taxation methods:

Declaration Method This is where taxpayers declare their income within a certain period. Generally, at the end of each year, taxpayers submit various account books to the local competent authority or collection agency for review by the Investigation Committee, which determines the tax based on the account books. However, the determination of the income amount must deduct this year's expenses, last year's surplus, various public taxes, insurance premiums, and reserve funds from the total income. This method requires a perfect accounting system; otherwise, there will be incidents of overreporting and collusion between officials and the public.

External Standard Estimation Method This is to estimate the amount of income based on external standards, and then calculate the amount of tax payable. The advantage of this method is that the procedures are relatively convenient and it can avoid the overreporting in the declaration method. However, there are also disadvantages, such as the difficulty in accurately and fairly estimating the work, and it is easy to collude and commit fraud.

Source Method This is used for salaries, rents, interest, etc., where the income has a definite source. It is extracted from the payer before the income is owned. The most obvious advantages of this method are reducing procedures, preventing tax evasion, and ensuring accurate amounts. However, there are also disadvantages. The result of separate taxation reduces the effectiveness of progressive tax rates.

The above three methods have both advantages and disadvantages. The method to adopt should be considered based on the specific circumstances of each country.

The Difference between Income Tax and Revenue Tax

What should be noted here is the distinction between income tax and revenue tax. There has been much debate over the two terms income tax and revenue tax; and on the surface, income and revenue seem similar, so they are often confused. However, if we can examine the nature of the two, it is not difficult to find their differences. Let's give a brief overview:

Although the tax sources of income tax and revenue tax are the same, the basis for taxation is different. Income tax is based on the income of people with income, while revenue tax is based on the revenue of things with income. Therefore, income tax is aimed at people and is called a personal tax, while revenue tax is aimed at things and is called a property tax. Naturally, it is difficult to strictly distinguish between people and things. Income tax is universal, and all income that meets the tax standards must be taxed. Revenue tax is not universal and is limited to certain specific revenues. The means of collecting revenue tax is general. It does not necessarily use net income as the standard, and often directly determines the tax amount based on gross revenue. Income tax must deduct various expenses and other public taxes paid by the person concerned in order to obtain such revenue, and only tax his net surplus income. In addition, income tax often takes into account various personal circumstances to determine different tax amounts, such as the difference between single and married people, and between those with and without debt.

The Evolution of the Income Tax Issue in China

Since income tax is a modern tax with abundant income, universal taxation, fair burden, and flexibility, most countries have already implemented it and are making increasing progress. It has occupied an important position in the tax system and is the main source of fiscal revenue. The earliest was the United Kingdom, which had already started collecting it in 1798; followed by the United States, which started in 1862; in addition, Italy, Germany, Japan, etc. all implemented it in the second half of the 19th century. Only France was later, deciding to adopt income tax in 1914 and officially implementing it in 1916. The following is a table listing the period of implementation of income tax in various countries and the percentage of income tax in total tax revenue (as of 1932):

As for China, although the call for collecting income tax had already been raised in the late Qing Dynasty, and the Republic of China has repeatedly decided to formulate regulations, until now, except for the collection of deformed party income donations from civil servants of various government agencies, it has not been formally implemented. The evolution of the income tax issue in the Republic of China can be summarized as follows:

According to investigation, at the beginning of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Finance, due to the financial difficulties of the national treasury, was determined to prepare for income tax, but it was repeatedly discussed and stopped, and no concrete plan was ever presented. In January of the third year, the 27 articles of the Income Tax Regulations were finally promulgated, and the estimated income was 2,175,000 yuan, which was added to the budget of the second year of the Republic of China, but it was not implemented. In August of the fourth year, because the scope of the originally established Income Tax Regulations was too broad and the procedures were too cumbersome, it was deeply felt that it was impossible to suddenly collect all kinds of income in the same period, so the first phase of the Income Tax Implementation Rules was formulated, preparing to promote it in stages, starting with officials, parliamentarians, and large businesses with more profits. It was decided that the former would be collected using the source method and the latter would be collected using the declaration method. The estimated budget number for the fifth year was included in 2,835,000 yuan, which seemed to have reached a concrete stage. Unexpectedly, in the end, it was still shelved due to domestic turmoil. In the eighth year of the Republic of China, the authorities felt that the tax rate of the first phase of the Implementation Rules was too high, and decided to abolish it. They formulated the amount of taxes to be collected in order and asked the provincial finance departments to estimate them separately, and stipulated that the income tax funds should be used for education and industry. In January of the tenth year of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Finance again announced the Implementation Rules of the Income Tax Regulations, the income tax collection tax items, the Income Tax Investigation and Review Committee Rules of Procedure, the Income Tax Collection Rules, the Income Tax Funds Storage and Allocation Regulations, etc. At that time, all provinces in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shandong, and Hubei had already determined the numbers. It was originally planned to be implemented from the first day of the month, but the provincial councils and chambers of commerce telegraphed to request a delay, which was extended for three months and eventually became indefinite.

After the establishment of the National Government, the discussion of collecting income tax arose again. In October of the 17th year of the Republic of China, the steps for handling income tax were stipulated. In January of the 18th year of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Finance revised and announced the Income Tax Regulations of the third year of the Republic of China, and revised the previous Income Tax Implementation Rules separately according to the main points of the revised regulations. However, after the promulgation of the revised regulations and implementation rules, actual collection was still not achieved. However, there is one thing we should pay attention to, that is, the income donation for civil servants implemented since the 16th year of the Republic of China, with an average monthly total of about 300,000 yuan. This indeed has a government official income tax similar to the income tax system, but the scope is too narrow after all, and the tax funds are used for local party departments, which has no relation to the central fiscal revenue, so it can only be regarded as a transitional deformed nature.

Until the summer of last year (24th year of the Republic of China), the government authorities finally felt that it was necessary to implement income tax in order to strengthen finance and improve the tax system. Therefore, they again consulted the previous established cases and drafted the new Provisional Regulations on Income Tax, totaling 31 articles. Initially, it was prepared to be implemented from July 1st, so 5 million yuan was included in the budget for the 24th year of the Republic of China; but it was decided to postpone it to January 1st of this year. However, the result is that it is still under discussion.

So, what is the reason for the delay? According to our investigation, it seems that it is roughly due to the following points: Political Disunity Incomplete Household Survey Lack of Bookkeeping Organization and other Technical Aspects Undeveloped Industry and Commerce Obstruction by Domestic Evil Forces Obstruction by Foreigners.

How to Implement it in the Future?

The above-mentioned obstacles have not been completely overcome now, and it is probably not very easy to resolve them in the near future. However, we cannot continue to follow the old ways. If we stubbornly wait for all the conditions to be met, hoping for a time without any difficulties, without making efforts to promote it, it is tantamount to waiting for a rabbit to bump into a tree, and there will never be a day to realize it.

So, how to implement it? Let us contribute some opinions:

Taxation Area Due to domestic political and economic constraints, and the difficulty of quickly completing the investigation work, it may not be possible to immediately implement a unified national income tax. It may be a good idea to change the method, collecting taxes by region; or starting with several provinces in the southeast, with the nature of a pilot project, improving it at any time, gradually expanding it, and finally promoting it to the whole country. However, the faster the promotion process, the better; otherwise, it will form a long-term inequality and the phenomenon of inter-provincial tax evasion. I believe that at most, it should be divided into four phases, with each phase lasting half a year. After two years, it must be popularized throughout the country. After two years of experience, various procedures should have a considerable clue, which will be easier than in the initial stage. Second, in order to avoid deliberate obstruction from various provinces to the central government, a certain percentage of the income tax funds may be allocated to local governments, so as to achieve the effect of cooperation between the central government and local governments. Although this is not in line with administrative unity and tax revenue unity, in special circumstances, it has to be regarded as a temporary transitional method in the absence of a better solution. However, if an extraordinary period is imminent, there is no need to be bound by the established phased procedure, and extraordinary means should be used to immediately promote it in all parts of the country.

Taxation Scope In the initial stage, various conditions are lacking, and it is impossible to cover all income at once, so it is necessary to promote it gradually. This is correct. However, the procedure can be researched. The scope of the recently promulgated Provisional Regulations on Income Tax is too narrow: The first category is the income of companies, shops, firms, factories, and temporary profit-making businesses; the second category is the income of salaries and remuneration; the most important asset income is not included here. Because land rents and house rents in asset income already have considerable local taxes (such as house donations, land taxes, and their surtaxes), it is true that income tax should be levied slowly before reaching a proper solution with the provinces (but excess income tax can be used for large landlords). However, the following types of income must be taxed at the same time, and it is not the most difficult technically: Income from government bond interest Income from deposit interest Dividend income of shareholders of large enterprises Excess income of the wealthy. If these incomes are not taxed, all the advantages of income tax, such as "universal collection," "fair burden," "sufficient income," and "flexibility," will be completely eliminated, and there will be no talk of using it as a source of emergency funds.

Taxation Method Due to the difficulty of investigation work and the fact that the taxation scope cannot cover all income at once, China cannot implement a comprehensive taxation system and should adopt a source taxation system, except for collecting excess income tax. As for how to tax when implementing source income tax, I think there is no need to stick to a single type, and it is better to choose a convenient and flexible one: Income from salaries and remuneration, and income from house rents can adopt the "source method;" income from companies, shops, firms, and factories with a more complete accounting organization can adopt the "declaration method;" income from freelance professionals and land rent can adopt the "external standard estimation method." In addition, the tax collection agency may entrust local governments and other existing tax collection agencies to collect or bring taxes on their behalf within the possible scope to save expenses.

Tax Rate At the beginning, the tax rate should not be too high or too low, and it should be closely related to the size of the income. The income tax regulations for the first category of profitable business income starting at 5% is appropriate, but the capital standard is set at 3,000 or more, which seems to be too burdensome for small businesses and should be changed to 5,000 yuan. The second category of salary and remuneration income starting at 600 yuan also seems to be too burdensome for small incomes and should be changed to 1,000 yuan. As for the starting point for tax, they are all set at 10 per mille, which is appropriate, but the progressive rate is too low, and the highest 200 per mille for large incomes would not be too harsh even if it were doubled. The aforementioned asset income tax and excess income tax should increase the tax rate further based on the principle of heavily taxing unearned income. In short, the burden on large income earners must be increased, which is naturally allowed during extraordinary periods. As for some people's claim that the tax rate should be differentiated based on the individual circumstances of the taxpayer, such as the number of family members and the existence of debt, China seems to be unable to consider this temporarily in the initial stage due to the complexity of the investigation work.

Relationship with other Taxes After the implementation of salary and remuneration income, the existing agency party income donations should be cancelled. All surtaxes on land and houses should be discussed with the provincial authorities to reduce or exempt them, and replace them with income tax in the short term. Business tax and other taxes that conflict too much with income tax should be adjusted. In addition, what should be implemented at the same time as income tax is inheritance tax.

Difficult Problems According to the above-mentioned methods, technical difficulties are secondary, and the most annoying is the obstruction of domestic evil forces and the restrictions of foreigners. The income in China, especially those with asset income, are directly or indirectly mostly powerful people. They try in every possible way to reduce the level of the progressive rate, and they must not include asset income in the scope of taxation. The reason why the recently promulgated regulations have such low levels and do not include asset income is also due to their activities to some extent. As for the foreign obstruction, it will often produce the phenomenon of tax evasion and even capital flight, which has a great impact on the future of China's income tax. The way to break this is not simply to eliminate all of them from the diplomatic perspective. The existing customs tax evasion problem has not yet been resolved, and the newly established income tax will inevitably have more trouble. Therefore, in order to make China's income tax progress smoothly, these two obstacles must be thoroughly eliminated, but it is not easy. Then, the taxpayers are generally small incomes that cannot be evaded, how can they be fair and universal?

In short, the necessity of China's income tax has been denied by anyone. The question is how to implement it? As for the issue of income tax and extraordinary finance, we naturally dare not assert that collecting income tax can solve the difficulties of extraordinary finance. But at least, it is an undeniable fact that income tax has a great auxiliary effect on extraordinary finance.

Review of Inheritance Tax 175

— Zeng Yun

Recently, the Ministry of Finance plans to levy income tax and inheritance tax. The former regulations have already been promulgated, and the latter are also under drafting. If there are no obstacles, they can be implemented. This is of course an important move in balancing national revenue and expenditure, and inheritance tax is the most reasonable and fair good tax under the modern private property system! Literally speaking, the so-called inheritance tax seems to be a very simple matter, just levying a certain amount of tax on the property left by someone. However, in practice, the procedures for levy and the standards for taxation are very complicated. It is one of the most difficult taxes to handle well. Even a slight omission can lead to adverse results.

Regarding the inheritance tax itself, there is a distinction between total inheritance tax and individual inheritance tax; regarding the geographical standard for taxation, there are differences based on the location of the property (inheritance location), based on the person (location of the deceased or heir), and based on nationality; regarding the object of the heir, there is a distinction between close relatives and distant relatives; regarding the standard of the tax rate, there are proportional tax rates and progressive tax rates, and within progressive tax rates, there is a difference between so-called full-amount progression and excess progression; in addition, the division of tax brackets, the provisions for tax exemption points, and those who are tax-exempt all require careful consideration and planning. To clarify the content of inheritance tax, it is necessary for us to briefly describe the above points.

Total inheritance tax and individual inheritance tax: the former taxes the total inheritance and has the nature of a property tax; the latter taxes each distribution of the inheritance and is in the nature of an unearned income tax. These two methods each have advantages and disadvantages. The total inheritance system simplifies the administrative procedures and saves collection costs, and the progressive rate increases relatively, and the tax-free amount decreases absolutely, which can increase tax revenue significantly. However, this contains an unfair element for the inheritance tax paying group, because taxing the total inheritance with the same standard will cause those who receive less to suffer a lot. On the other hand, the individual inheritance system must separately stipulate whether there is a tax-free amount and the level of the progressive rate. The procedure is cumbersome, but from the perspective of the inheritance beneficiary class, the burden seems fairer. Currently, various countries, such as Japan and Germany, purely adopt the individual inheritance system (Germany created a total inheritance system in 1919, but abolished it after 1922 and included it in the individual inheritance system), while the United Kingdom and France adopt both total and individual systems. The United States has the total inheritance tax under federal jurisdiction and the individual inheritance tax under state jurisdiction. It is said that only British Columbia (British Columbia) solely adopts the total inheritance system.

Geographical Standard of Taxation This is the most troublesome issue in the collection of inheritance tax. When inheritance is transferred, complex situations often arise where the deceased and the heirs are located in different places. Therefore, there are many tax standards. Some are based on the address of the deceased, some are based on the address of the heir, some are based on the nationality of the deceased, and some are based on the location of the property. The interpretation of the address of the deceased and the heir varies from place to place, so there are often instances of double taxation. Sometimes, the same property is taxed in location A, location B, and even location C. This phenomenon is most common in the United States. The laws of each state in the United States do not uniformly interpret the geographical standard, so sometimes when the deceased is in state A, the heir is in state B, and the inheritance is in state C, states A, B, and C can each levy taxes according to their own tax rates. As for solely using the location of the property as the standard, it is indeed much clearer, but it is not without problems. For example, if someone leaves stocks of a certain company, and the company has property in several places, then the situation becomes complicated. In addition, due to differences in international legislation, it is often impossible to avoid the phenomenon of double taxation of inheritance tax. Although various countries are currently trying to find ways to eliminate this difficulty, they have not found a reliable solution because international coordination has not been universal and thorough.

Relationship Between the Deceased and the Heirs The inheritance tax rates in most countries are based on the closeness of the relationship between the deceased and the heirs, with distant relatives being taxed more than close relatives. They believe that close relatives are entitled to it, while distant relatives are incidental. France divides into eleven classes, the United Kingdom divides into five classes, and Japan distinguishes between family head inheritance and general inheritance, with the tax rate for family head inheritance being lower than that for general inheritance. The above-mentioned method of dividing into classes for taxation is undoubtedly accurate and fair among inheritance tax payers. However, it also has considerable shortcomings, namely, the procedures are too troublesome. Because of the distinction between close and distant relatives, the standards for tax exemption amounts, the level of progressive rates, etc., must be stipulated separately. What is likely to happen is to increase the tax evasion by cunning people. For example, the inheritance that distant relatives should receive can often be represented by close relatives in name to enjoy a lighter tax rate.

Standard of Tax Rates Making the tax rate appropriate is another heavy task. The standards on which tax rates are based generally include the following: the size of the inheritance tax; that is, according to the amount of the inheritance, divide it into several classes, each class specifying a different tax rate, generally using a progressive method to increase it, and stipulating a minimum point and a maximum point. The relationship between the deceased and the heirs; as mentioned above, some also differentiate into several different tax brackets based on the degree of kinship. Whether there are children or how many there are; this is probably a special development under the social policy of encouraging population growth. The inheritance tax laws in France have different tax rates depending on whether there are children or how many there are. Those with four children can even be exempted from total inheritance tax. In addition, there is the so-called determination of the tax rate based on the turnover of the inheritance, such as the Italian E. Rignano, who advocated that the first inheritance tax rate should be the lightest, and the second and third times... the rate would gradually increase. However, this method is close to an ideal, and there are many practical difficulties, so no country has adopted it. First, the original property and the newly added property after inheritance are easily mixed together and cannot be accurately identified; second, the previous heir may deliberately consume the original property under the inheritance; third, the price of property changes indefinitely, which will affect future tax relations. As for the pre-payment method advocated by the Englishman Daton, that is, the first heir, in addition to paying the inheritance tax that he should originally bear, will also pre-pay the tax amount for the second inheritance, and the state will give a considerable interest every year before the second inheritance is implemented; although this is already more concrete, it may not be easy to handle.

Full Progression vs. Excess Progression Generally speaking, taxation is divided into proportional tax rates and progressive tax rates, but the inheritance tax method is ultimately progressive. This is because the direct tax of inheritance tax is unearned income, and only by levying it at a progressive tax rate can true fairness be achieved. However, there is a distinction between full progression (adopted by the United Kingdom, Germany, etc.) and excess progression (adopted by France, Japan, the United States, etc.) in the progressive method. The advantages and disadvantages of the two are mutually evident. Full progression is simpler and generates more revenue, but it has an unfair phenomenon; excess progression is the opposite. For example: the amount of A's inheritance is 20,000 yuan, and the tax rate is 1%, so the tax payable is 200 yuan, and the actual amount is 19,800 yuan; the amount of B's inheritance is 20,010 yuan, and the tax rate is 1.5%. If calculated according to full amount progression, the tax payable is 300 yuan and 15 cents, and the actual amount is 19,699 yuan and 85 cents, the actual amount of the latter is less than that of the former. However, the excess progressive levy is different, that is, 20,010 yuan, 10,000 yuan is calculated according to the 1% tax rate, the tax amount is 200 yuan, and only 10 yuan is calculated according to 1.5%, the tax amount is 15 cents, totaling 200 yuan and 15 cents, and the actual amount can be 19,809 yuan and 85 cents.

Scope of Tax The standards for the provision of tax-free scope are roughly the following: (1) Based on the amount of inheritance: that is, the law stipulates a tax-free standard point. Those who are less than a certain amount are tax-free, and those who exceed a certain amount are taxed at a rate. There are many ways to implement it: some stipulate that if the amount of inheritance exceeds the set tax-free point, the entire inheritance will be taxed, and the original tax-free amount will no longer be deducted (adopted by Japan, Germany, etc.), and some only tax the excess part, such as if the amount of inheritance is 4,000 yuan and the tax-free point is 3,000 yuan, then only the excess part of 1,000 yuan will be taxed, and 3,000 yuan will be excluded (adopted by the United States, France, etc.). There is also the so-called Vanishing exemption, such as if the original tax-free point is 3,000 yuan, but if it exceeds 1 yuan, 1 yuan will be reduced. At this time, the tax-free amount becomes 1,999 yuan, and the taxable inheritance is 2 yuan. When the excess amount reaches 3,000 yuan (that is, when the inheritance amount is 6,000 yuan), the tax-free amount will be cancelled, and the entire 6,000 yuan will be taxed (adopted by the Federation of South Africa, etc.). (2) Determined according to the nature of the inheritance beneficiary; if the inheritance is donated to charity and other public undertakings, it is generally tax-free. (3) Determined according to the number of children; this is a special treatment under the social policy of a country. For example, France, in order to encourage population growth, exceptionally gives tax reductions or exemptions to those with more children. (4) Determined according to the nature of the deceased; that is, the inheritance of personnel who died in action or were injured and died due to battlefield service in the army, navy, and air force is exempt from tax.

Object of Inheritance The types of inheritance can include all real and personal property, land, houses, inventory, cash, deposits, loans, bills, accounts receivable, interest receivable, as well as certificates representing property interests or business profits, commercial, patent rights, trademark rights, copyright, etc. However, when taxing, the debts of the deceased, unpaid mortgages, and various taxes and public charges payable should be deducted, as well as insurance premiums, funeral expenses, necessary expenses for managing and distributing the inheritance and executing the will, as well as accidental losses, etc. As for whether the education expenses of minor heirs should be deducted, it depends on the education policy of each country.

The above points are important items that must be understood when discussing inheritance tax issues; as for how to implement it, there is naturally no fixed mechanical standard, and it must be considered according to the actual situation of each country.

Now, let us further look at the draft inheritance tax regulations drafted by the Ministry of Finance. Combining the contents of each chapter and article, the most important points can be obtained as follows:

(1) Abandoning the individual inheritance system and adopting the total inheritance system;

(2) Taxing regardless of the closeness of inheritance;

(3) Adopting the location of the property in the country and nationality abroad as the standard for taxation;

(4) Setting the tax-free point at 3,000 yuan, but the Executive Yuan revised it to 5,000 yuan after review;

(5) Adopting the excess progressive system, with a minimum of 1% and a maximum of 24%, but those exceeding 10 million yuan will be taxed at 5% for each additional million yuan;

Organize an inheritance review committee; Let us briefly review the above six points:

The advantages and disadvantages of the individual inheritance system and the total inheritance system have been mentioned above, but China should temporarily adopt the total inheritance system. At present, China's financial and administrative technology is backward, so it should avoid being overly meticulous; China's property system and will system have not yet been popularized, and the collection procedures of the individual inheritance system are too complicated; China does not yet have a property tax. If the individual inheritance system is implemented, it seems too abrupt in the procedure, and the total inheritance system can also fulfill the task of a property tax. However, no matter whether the total inheritance system or the individual inheritance system is adopted, a sound household registration system is a necessary prerequisite. If China's household registration census cannot be completed precisely, it will hinder the collection of inheritance tax, which is extremely serious.

Inheritance is originally unearned income, and in reality, there is no such thing as entitled or incidental. Therefore, when taxing, it is indeed not necessary to distinguish between the closeness of inheritance. Moreover, as mentioned above, China's financial and administrative technology has not been sound, and these complicated classification tasks are difficult to undertake. It is still possible that various malpractices will occur in the future, such as concealment of tax evasion, etc.; it is better to abandon complexity and choose simplicity.

The taxation standard excludes the address, and adopts the location of the property in the country and nationality abroad: as explained in the draft regulations, it has the advantage of combining the advantages of both personal and territorial principles, and can avoid the drawbacks of mutual discrimination in various places. However, there are still things that have not been clearly stated and have become questions, such as the company stocks with property in several places mentioned above, which place should be used as the standard? In addition, whether the taxation of the inheritance of foreigners in China can proceed smoothly is probably still a problem.

Whether the tax-free point of 3,000 yuan or 5,000 yuan is a compromise in principle, but whether it is necessary to reconsider it in light of the current distribution of property among the Chinese people is another question. However, whether the education expenses of adult heirs should be deducted and included in the tax-free list is not mentioned in the draft regulations. In my humble opinion, since China's free education has not yet been popularized, it seems that a deduction should be added.

The excess progressive rate is fairer, which is undoubtedly undeniable; but in my humble opinion, it is not necessary to mechanically and completely treat everyone the same. It seems unnecessary to give this kind of preferential treatment to those with larger inheritance amounts. The full amount progressive rate can be used for those above 100,000 yuan, and the excess progressive rate can still be used for those below 100,000 yuan, that is, both the full amount progressive system and the excess progressive system can be adopted. As for the progressive rate, the set rate is also too low, and it may be appropriate to increase it slightly. I hope that the legislative authorities will study it in detail during the review.

The review committee is a necessary institution, but its work is very complicated; if the investigation and evaluation work is missed, it will not only affect government tax revenue, but also often produce corruption phenomena. Especially the valuation of land, houses, goodwill, patent rights, trademark rights, copyright, etc., is even more difficult. In addition, it is also very possible for the review committee and taxpayers to collude in fraud.

In short, inheritance tax is the best of all taxes, but it is also the most difficult to handle precisely and thoroughly. China's inheritance tax is still in its infancy, and the difficulties encountered must be many. Now we put forward the minimum hope: the tax rate is not too low; the investigation and evaluation must be accurate; we must absolutely prevent fraud and tax evasion; we must eliminate all unreasonable obstacles, and implement it as soon as possible; the tax revenue should be used for proper construction and educational undertakings. Finally, I have to reiterate that if the household registration census cannot be done thoroughly, I am afraid that the results of inheritance tax collection will not be optimistic.

Special Issue of Shanghai Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Publicity Week

Eradicating Opium and National Rejuvenation 178

— Pan Gongzhan

The strong bully the weak, the chaotic are insulted and perish. These are ancient Chinese idioms; survival of the fittest, natural selection, these are modern social evolution theories. Corruption breeds worms. Although this is not logically correct in science, it has considerable truth in meaning. Therefore, if a person wants to have a considerable position in society, to be self-reliant and not be eliminated, the basic conditions are to work hard, strive, and not have weaknesses that can be attacked by others; otherwise, if one cannot be invigorated and merely hopes to survive by luck, one will eventually tend towards failure. This is true for individuals, and it is also true for countries and nations.

The strength of modern countries does not depend on the hard work of a few people, but is created by the vast majority of outstanding people in the country. In the past, power was concentrated in the hands of a few people or the emperor. If the few people or the emperor were wise and enlightened, the country could become strong at any time, because the absolute majority of the people were ignorant and obedient and listened to the commands of one person or a few people. If the emperor or a few people were foolish and incompetent, the country would also decline. The historical records of the rise and fall of dynasties and the prosperity and decline of nations are mostly due to this reason. However, in modern countries, power is in the hands of the majority of the people, and the fate of the country and nation depends on the quality of each member that constitutes the country and nation. If the members of the organization are not good, then the entire organization will not be sound. For example, in the human body, how can one expect the whole body to be healthy if the cells are not healthy? Although Germany was defeated in the European War, it regained its position in Europe today in less than twenty years. Some say that it was Hitler's hard work and determination that enabled Germany to revive. However, this is just a superficial observation. Without the support of the excellent German nation, even if Hitler held power, it would only be for a few years. Even with natural talent and strong will, how could he enable the once-defeated German nation to re-enter the ranks of European powers in the shortest possible time?

Since the Opium War, the majority of the Chinese people have been immersed in the atmosphere of opium and drugs for nearly a century. In these hundred years, I don't know how many aspiring young people have been buried, and I don't know how many promising people have been buried. The impoverishment of individuals and the decline of the national spirit are all due to opium and drugs. In the early years of the Republic of China, although there were several strict prohibitions, the opium and drug problem continued to spread and the area widened, because the prohibitors were not determined and the smokers did not understand the harm. Those who smoked only opium in the past gradually became more severe, and red pills and morphine gradually became widespread. They can go without food, but they cannot live without opium and drugs; they can not plant rice, but they cannot plant poppies. Those who smoke opium and drugs are directly harmed, and those who do not smoke opium and drugs are also indirectly greatly affected. If this continues, China will inevitably decline even if it is not invaded; even if the powers do not divide it, we will never be able to survive. With such a corrupt and unprogressive nation, if we want to compete on the stage of the 20th century with self-improving and excellent nations, there is no reason to survive. People must insult themselves before others insult them, and the country must attack itself before others attack it. The spread of opium and drugs is equivalent to the suicide of the entire nation. Not only is there no hope of revival, but it will also be forever in an irreversible position. Poland was destroyed, but it can be revived; Turkey was the sick man of the Near East, but it can also be revitalized. However, the reason for their revival and revitalization is that the people are aware of the pain of national destruction, and they can gather, teach, and train, so that they can jump out of the shackles of the powers after the European War. If the majority of the people in the country are addicted to opium and drugs and are confused and lost, even if there is an opportunity, how can they save themselves? Lin Zexu said that after ten years, there will be no available soldiers and no people who can be used. Under the current national situation, without waiting for ten years, the country will be slaughtered by others. Now the powers are preparing their troops and horses to prepare for the arrival of the second world war and re-divide the colonies. Our country has great rivers and mountains, and strong neighbors have been watching for a long time. If we do not seek progress and strive to improve ourselves, the imperialists can take advantage of the pretext of civilization and swallow us up.

China has now reached the last moment of life and death. The revival of the country and nation depends on the results of our final efforts. However, how can the nation be revived? Although there are various conditions, the minimum is to first eradicate the opium and drugs that destroy the country and reduce the population. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has set a three-year plan to ban drugs and a six-year plan to ban opium, and strictly implemented it. This is really the only way to save the country. Because if opium and drugs are not eradicated for a day, the Chinese nation will never have the hope of revival; if opium and drugs are not purified for a day, the Chinese nation will be forever in the dark hell. Opium and drugs are demons that destroy lofty ambitions, opium and drugs are tools that corrupt the spirit, opium and drugs are shackles that bind thoughts, and opium and drugs are sharp weapons that cut the body. Smoking opium and drugs will not only harm oneself, but will also harm future generations. Therefore, for the sake of personal future, for the sake of the development of future generations, and for the sake of the survival of the entire nation, we must strictly eradicate opium and drugs, and we must resolutely quit opium and drugs!

Overview of the Bureau's Anti-Smoking Measures in the Past Six Months 179

— Cai Jinjun

It is well known that opium is harmful to everyone. Since the late Qing dynasty and throughout the decades of the Republic of China, detailed criminal laws and strict prohibitions have been established. However, in reality, the results have been insignificant, and the harm has become increasingly severe. Why is this? It is simply because the enforcement of the prohibition has not been effective. This city is a major commercial port connecting China and foreign countries, the transportation hub of the nation, with a dense population and a flourishing commerce. Many citizens are accustomed to luxury and indulgence. Lawless individuals take advantage of the convenient transportation and the lack of unified police authority to secretly establish manufacturing or storage dens, transporting and selling opium for personal gain. If we do not urgently plan for a thorough eradication, it will not only harm this area but also affect the implementation of the national anti-smoking policy. Our mayor attaches great importance to the eradication of opium and drugs in this city and is determined to completely eliminate them. I, Jinjun, am in charge of public security and have been ordered to oversee anti-smoking measures concurrently. Although my achievements in the past six months have been insignificant, I feel deeply ashamed. Now, I am writing this article in response to the call for submissions by the preparatory committee for anti-smoking and anti-drug propaganda. I would like to briefly describe the general situation of the Bureau's anti-smoking efforts.

I have always believed that the harm of opium and drugs in our country is so deep that it cannot be eradicated in the short term. Therefore, the late Premier's instructions determined the anti-smoking plan, formulated a six-year anti-smoking program, promulgated orders to eliminate various illegal activities within a time limit, and supervised the provinces and cities to vigorously promote the program. When the Bureau received the order to implement the anti-smoking program in July of the 24th year, we immediately began the first step of registering opium addicts. We believe that prohibiting cultivation, transportation, and sale must be based on prohibiting addiction. The registration of opium addicts aims to obtain the total number of opium addicts and create statistics to serve as a standard for the annual reduction and control of cultivation, transportation, and sale. Therefore, the registration must be universal, and the statistics on opium consumption must be accurate. With accurate statistics on opium addicts and opium consumption, we can set the annual reduction standards. Once the reduction standards are set, we can control the production and sales of opium. As opium addicts gradually decrease, the production, transportation, and sale of opium should also decrease proportionally. When opium addicts are completely abstinent, cultivation, transportation, and sale should be completely prohibited. This approach, which links the prohibition of cultivation, transportation, sale, and addiction, is more effective and well-intentioned than previous enforcement methods and can be confidently anticipated.

Therefore, at the beginning of the Bureau's anti-smoking efforts, the focus of our work was entirely on the registration of opium addicts. From July to December of the 24th year, we registered a total of 30,833 opium addicts. The table is as follows:

According to the table above, the area with the most severe opium and drug problem in this city is the jurisdiction of the Lao Beimen Police Station, followed by the Yi Miao Police Station. The area with the least severe problem is the central urban area. This is a noteworthy point because the areas closer to rural areas have a lighter opium and drug problem, while the densely populated areas have a more severe problem. The social reasons for this phenomenon are worth our study. As for the age statistics of registered opium addicts, the 40 to 50 age group is the largest, followed by the 30 to 40 age group. The 30 to 50 age group is the most important period of life, when people are establishing their careers. Addiction leads to the unseen waste of useful talents. What is the impact on society and the nation? The age statistics of opium addicts are listed below:

Age Number of People

Under 20 years old 17

21 to 30 years old 2248 31 to 40 years old 9468

As mentioned above, the main purpose of registering opium addicts is to obtain the total number of opium addicts and the total amount of opium consumed. According to the Bureau's statistics on opium consumption, the majority of opium addicts consume one to two qian per day, followed by two to three qian. There are also as many as 26 people who consume more than one liang per day. In total, 30,833 opium addicts were registered, consuming 6373.832 liang of opium paste per day, with an average of more than two qian per person. If each liang of opium paste is calculated at two yuan, then the daily cost is more than 12,747 yuan, and the annual consumption is 4.5 million yuan. This is based on the opium consumption of the first group of registered opium addicts, and the actual number is even higher. What is the impact of this huge amount of money being spent on opium on the national economy and the people's livelihood? This is only in terms of direct consumption. As for the farmland used for opium cultivation, it reduces the production of food crops, leading to the import of foreign food and the outflow of huge amounts of money. The indirect losses cannot be estimated. Therefore, if the harm of opium is not eliminated, the national economy and agricultural production will inevitably suffer, and there will be no way to save the situation. From an economic standpoint, the importance of the anti-smoking problem can be imagined.

The licenses for quitting opium within a time limit are divided into two types: for the poor and for ordinary people. Among those who obtained ordinary licenses from the Bureau, there were 10,387 men and 2,451 women, for a total of 12,838 people. Among those who obtained licenses for the poor, there were 15,364 men and 2,631 women, for a total of 17,995 people. Comparing the two, the number of people with licenses for the poor exceeds the number of people with ordinary licenses by more than 5,000. Logically speaking, opium addiction is something that only those with financial resources can afford. The income of the poor is already insufficient for their daily expenses, so where would they have the extra money for unnecessary consumption? However, in reality, there are more poor people who are addicted to opium than wealthy people. What is the reason for this? This is also worth our study.

According to the population statistics in the Bureau's jurisdiction, there are a total of 2,011,814 people. The ratio of registered opium addicts to the population is 1.5%. This does not include those who have not been registered, those who have quit on their own, and those who have been arrested for opium addiction and sent to rehabilitation centers. According to the estimates of the special industry association in this city, there should be 120,000 opium addicts in this city. Therefore, those who have registered according to the regulations are only one-third of the total number of opium addicts. If we follow the estimates of the special industry association, the ratio of opium addicts to the population in this city is at least 5.4%, meaning that at least five out of every hundred people are opium addicts. Now, the methods for reporting opium addicts for registration have been promulgated. During the reporting period, opium addicts are allowed to register retroactively. In the future, the number of registered opium addicts will increase, and the ratio of opium addicts to the population will change. Therefore, this ratio cannot be determined at this time.

From July to December of last year, the Bureau sent a total of 4,304 opium addicts to various rehabilitation hospitals. Among them, 1,167 men and 284 women were detoxified at the Hu Nan Rehabilitation Hospital, 2,134 men were detoxified at the Hu Bei Rehabilitation Hospital, 253 men and 32 women were detoxified at the temporary detoxification center, and 363 men and 71 women were detoxified at the prisoner rehabilitation hospital. The number of people detoxified at the rehabilitation hospitals designated by the Bureau and the Health Bureau is not included. Analyzing the reasons for the enthusiasm of opium addicts to quit opium, it is due to the fact that some opium addicts have a thorough understanding of the government's anti-smoking policy and have therefore awakened. However, it is also because opium detoxification is completely free in this city, so some people voluntarily report for detoxification. Another group of people are afraid of the severe penalties under the provisional regulations on anti-smoking and punishment, and therefore voluntarily request detoxification. However, from our point of view, it is gratifying if opium addicts have a clear understanding of the government's anti-smoking policy. Even if they request detoxification out of fear of punishment, it is also commendable. Therefore, we believe that the enthusiasm of opium addicts to request detoxification brings endless hope for the future of anti-smoking efforts.

Regarding the investigation of opium cases in the 24th year, the number of cases solved is higher than in previous years due to the Bureau's strict investigation. From January to the end of December of last year, a total of 2,215 cases of private opium use were solved, involving 3,981 first-time male offenders, 490 female offenders, 9 male repeat offenders, and 1 female offender with three offenses, for a total of 3,990 men and 491 women. 652.27 liang of opium were seized. A total of 111 cases of private opium sales were solved, involving 128 male offenders and 24 female offenders. 149.5 liang of opium were seized. A total of 36 cases of private opium transportation were solved, involving 44 male offenders and 4 female offenders. 2,495.36 liang of opium were seized. A total of 166 cases of privately set up opium dens were solved, involving 241 male offenders and 33 female offenders. 91.94 liang of opium were seized. In the above statistical figures, the number of cases of private opium use is the highest, indicating that opium addicts are not fully aware of the anti-smoking laws. This is probably due to the weak foundation of national education. As for the cases of private opium sales, 101 cases were solved before July of last year, and 10 cases were solved after July. From the numerical perspective, it can be seen that the investigation of private opium sales is stricter than before July, making private opium sellers afraid to make a living from this activity. Therefore, the number of private opium sales cases solved has decreased significantly compared to before, which is something we are very pleased about.

The above is a general overview of the Bureau's anti-smoking efforts. Due to space limitations, I cannot list everything in detail. Recently, the Bureau's work has focused on reporting opium addicts for registration. During the reporting period, opium addicts are allowed to register retroactively. This is because the government is compassionate and giving opium addicts an opportunity to reform. However, the deadline is March. We hope that opium addicts who have not yet registered will quickly go to the Bureau to apply for registration and not miss the opportunity, lest they fall into the net of the law. I, Jinjun, am incompetent and have not been able to implement the anti-smoking policy perfectly. I respectfully ask for guidance from members of society so that the advancement of anti-smoking efforts can be more effective and can be completed as scheduled. This would not only be my personal good fortune but also the blessing of the nation and the people.

Supplement to the "Shen Bao" Local News

Talking Points

Has Abyssinia Not Failed? 180

— Jian Ping

The Italian imperialist war of aggression against Abyssinia, which has lasted for more than half a year, has now resulted in the Italian army winning victory after victory by using various illegal and cruel tactics, due to Abyssinia's isolation and helplessness. According to confirmed war reports, the Italian army has captured the city of Taixi in Abyssinia and is stepping up its advance towards the Abyssinian capital. It can be seen that the Italian-Abyssinian war has reached its final stage. However, at this time when the situation in Europe and the Far East is very awkward, the relationship between imperialist powers is becoming more and more complex. Everyone is very willing to see the Abyssinian war end as soon as possible, and even at the expense of sacrificing the small and weak nations that have been invaded in order to please the Italian Empire. Therefore, the League of Nations, which had once argued red-facedly for sanctions against Italy, has also changed its tune to "the issue of peace talks between Italy and Abyssinia." From this, we can more clearly see the true face of imperialism.

However, the issue of peace talks is not enough to satisfy the ambitious and constantly victorious Italian Empire. Therefore, at the Thirteen-Nation Conference on the 16th, the Italian representative put forward the pre-conditions for the resolution: 1. The Abyssinian army must disarm and show submission. 2. The Abyssinian king must be deposed. 3. The Italian army must occupy the Abyssinian capital. 4. The railway from the French territory of Djibouti to the Abyssinian capital must be specially supervised by the Italian army. In other words, the Italian Empire is unwilling to negotiate peace until Abyssinia is destroyed. Abyssinia, which is bravely resisting the enemy, certainly cannot accept such conditions of national subjugation. The "resolute refusal" of the Abyssinian delegation was expected. The Thirteen-Nation Conference had no choice but to declare the peace talks a failure.

After the failure of the peace talks, the natural course of action is for Italian imperialism to launch a more active and cruel offensive against the Abyssinian capital. Imperialist wars of aggression do not hesitate to use all illegal tactics, and the danger of the Abyssinian capital is inevitable. However, Abyssinia, which is bravely resisting the enemy, will not yield, and their war will not stop because of violence. A dispatch from the Abyssinian capital on the 17th said that the Abyssinian government will move its capital to Biro, 125 miles west of the Abyssinian capital, if necessary. From this, we can see the determination of Abyssinia to resist the enemy. Even if Abyssinia is defeated, we believe that it is glorious and victorious. This is because the success or failure of a thing cannot be concluded based on temporary victories or defeats.

Husband and Wife 181

— Bai Ling

—At the Foot of Laoshan Mountain—

In the warm sunshine, that gray Haiqi warship left the Qingdao pier, and on the calm blue sea, it floated along a series of continuous mountains.

The sea in spring is beautiful. The mountains of Qingdao in spring are also beautiful.

After a short voyage, the hazy peak of Laoshan Mountain, which towered high into the clouds, appeared like a large ancient tomb.

Small mountains surrounded it, undulating.

Small boats, each holding only twenty people, lowered from the warship, began to row busily towards the rocky shore.

On the winding, sheep-gut-like, flat mountain road, an uneven team of us, tall and short, wearing light blue uniforms, crawled along, heading straight for the Huayan Temple.

After resting at the Huayan Temple, we dispersed.

At this time, I and three classmates were excitedly hopping around. After visiting the nearby scenic spots, we were really tired, and our feet no longer had the strength to trek. We walked step by step towards a small mountain village. This mountain village had only five households. The small houses were all built of uneven yellow stones, and the roofs were covered with thatch. Around this mountain village was a mountain, and on the left was a vast sea, but there was no farmland. Everywhere was a desolate scene.

We stood behind a house in this mountain village. We couldn't see a single person. Flocks of chickens clucking "cluck, cluck" were scratching around on the hillside. The mountain village was quiet.

Suddenly, from the small road in the south of the village, a man in his thirties walked over. The man's face was long and a bit yellow. He was not wearing a hat, and his head was bald. He was wearing a patched old blue cloth gown, and he looked like someone who didn't work. He walked up to us, glanced at us, didn't stop, and hurriedly walked into a courtyard. We were just about to leave this village when suddenly, a burst of irritable scolding came from the courtyard where the man had just entered: "Damn it, you're so brave!" Followed by a woman's crying. The courtyard became uneasy. A man who was no more than thirty years old ran out of the courtyard, chased by the man we had met. He ran while looking back. But the person chasing him from behind, chased and cursed: "I'll screw your ancestors, if you come again, I'll break your dog legs..." As if he was touched by something, he stopped chasing and immediately turned around and ran into the courtyard. As soon as he entered the courtyard, he raised his voice: "I'm asking you, I'm asking you, do you dare again?" His fist seemed to be punching the woman. The woman pleaded, raising her throat: "I, I, I dare not again..."

The man hit again: "Hey, damn you... what do I keep you for, you're really going to kill me! You're so brave, you're sneaking around with other people when I'm not home... I'm going to beat you, beat you, how much did you get from them? Tell me, tell me?"

The woman sobbed: "I, I, only three times..." After a while: "You have to think about it too, you don't care about me, you're hooking up with other people's women outside, not coming home for three or two months, what am I supposed to eat? Look at other people's men, how capable they are, who's like you... when the spring is warm, everyone goes up the mountain to look for business, haven't you seen how lively the mountains have been these days, the gentlemen, ladies, young masters, and young ladies from Qingdao all come to visit the mountains, you should find a partner, carry a sedan chair up the mountain to take a look... you don't learn to be good, and you come to scold me, beat me, I, I, I was forced to, I had no choice, that's why..."

The man didn't say a word. After a long time, he said: "Damn you, you have no right to interfere with my business, I'm going to beat you, you, you, how much money did he give you? Tell me, tell me, take it out..."

Page 18

Abandonment 182

— Xu Ji

The night was dark and deep, and a smoky fog rose at the far end of the street. The wind was blowing incessantly, so sharp and piercing. Fine rain fell quietly like dust…

The street bared its dark and glossy surface, and pedestrians passed by intermittently, one or two at a time. The street was vast and wide. In a corner, the dim light shone on the porch of a house, vaguely revealing a few characters eroded by time: "Xiaoying Tang" (Infant Asylum).

(Infant asylum! There, from a young age, people are constantly suffering a miserable fate, forgetting human love and laughter, and accumulating endless hatred of life...)

Then, from the fine rain, from the distance of the street, a broken black shadow floated: swaying, blurred and weak...

On the night street with fine rain and thick fog, this time, he really mustered up the courage to come here! Before, he had come here alone once or twice to visit, looking at something, thinking about something, deciding something—but this time, really, it was no longer just him alone, but two people! Two people! (He looked at the fragile little life in his arms. Yes, now there were two people!)

His hands trembling, he looked again and again at the little life sleeping in his arms, wrapped in broken bedding, breathing lightly like the evening breeze, carrying a stubborn, cramping will to live: this life had finally come into the world: no one had the right to control its life again, but did people have the right to put it into a miserable fate? That howling, that writhing, that sleeping posture of the baby...

Looking at the dark drawer on the wall of the infant asylum, he trembled violently as if he had been touched by something harmful: there, a person's eternal fate would be buried; there, a soul's eternal laughter would be buried: there, it was a tomb, a terrible blood mouth that devoured people's childhood laughter...

In the cold wind of the night, tears fell sparsely: thinking of the young wife's weeping a few hours earlier, his heart felt like it was being twisted - a wave of sinful regret pierced deeply into his heart, painful, hateful; "Why? Why in the face of life, even the birth of a small life has become the greatest crime? Why should the enthusiasm between people be subjected to such cruel, unforgivable, painful punishments...?"

Destroy it, destroy that miserable little life, and perhaps that will end all the pain of the human world for it; however, thinking of himself, what right did he have to let it die, "Maybe it will grow up; maybe it will change the fate of the world; maybe..."

Thinking that way, his heart gradually became clear and calm. He had been wandering in the fine rain for a while, and the cold wind was blowing his thin clothes, and he was getting wet. He shivered, hugged the little life in his arms tightly again, and gently repented: "Child, you must forgive us in the face of life!" Then, he quickly walked to the corner of the wall, pulled open the big drawer, and quickly put the child in. In an instant, a lonely shadow slipped away on the other side of the street. The street was dark and quiet. The alarm bell of the big drawer rang "Dang", and then the people in the "Baby Receiving Office" inside habitually took the child out: "Ah, another one! We have to register it!"

The registrar registered on the book stroke by stroke, deciding a person's future fate stroke by stroke...

The night was cold and humid, but the tears of the departing person had dried.

Mr. Ziming 183

— Shi Feng

The spring sunshine warmly shone on Mr. Ziming's gray-white hair, and the two shiny spectacle frames, lonely reflected a weak silver light. Holding a tattered book in his hand, he read with his head shaking. The spectacle frames moved and reflected the light.

His eyes were already blurry. Even wearing reading glasses made it difficult to read. Not only that, his body was bent like a bow. When he stood up, he looked small, his skin was brown, and he looked like a dried-up old man made of wood carvings! However, some of his movements, although clumsy, were sometimes very childish. Sometimes, he would childishly recall and practice the movements of the past, but that would only make himself or others laugh.

He was old. Like the tattered books in his hands…

Those books lonely accompanied him throughout his life. From a very young age, he loved books. He didn't have money to buy books at home, so he borrowed them from others. ——That often resulted in rejection or cold looks. His mother didn't know who she was fooled by, giving her hard-earned money to her child to study, hoping that he would definitely get his money back in the future. Seeing that he had finished reading the Four Books and the Classics, the system was changed at that time; he entered the local higher normal school for free, from which he could become a teacher. A teacher, what a noble profession!

At school, he fell in love with painting. Especially landscape painting in Chinese painting. This doesn't mean that he specialized in painting, he still studied other subjects as usual. Due to his mother's urging and his own efforts, his studies exceeded the level of others, and his landscape painting was even more eye-catching.

So when he graduated, there was no major problem with his job. He chose a position in a middle school and an elementary school in his hometown. He often said that a person should contribute some effort to his hometown, even if that effort is not necessarily great, or even beneficial to his hometown.

At school, the students showed him respect and love. He also guided the students as if he loved his own children.

Especially his paintings, many people came to ask for them; in an era when civil wars broke out one after another, Mr. Ziming's hometown had no way to escape this big vortex. Today, the county magistrate was just changed, and tomorrow, who knew who would be the county magistrate; in that era, his paintings were even more popular: the county magistrates must have him paint them, as a souvenir. We know that when a county magistrate took office, those local gentlemen would all go to curry favor with him, so they came to ask Mr. Ziming to help them, to paint a picture, just any picture, to "commemorate" it. Who knew that after agreeing to it, his fame would grow? This school invited him, that school invited him, and those county magistrates who had retired from office also started schools, and even more fervently invited him.

He was a scholar, with a very strong literati flavor. He tried to find ways to refuse these invitations. He didn't leave his hometown, he was willing to serve the local area.

Later, when the children grew up and the mother got old, he couldn't move even more, so he guarded the home.

He watched himself getting old. One autumn, he suffered another serious illness. After he recovered, his body was as thin as a scarecrow made of a few sorghum stalks, with almost no flesh. At this time, he decided to stop working and recuperate at home, painting a little in the future to exchange for money to live on. But those students who respected and loved him did not allow him to resign, and they waited for him to come to school with their classes empty. This act of kindness made him shed tears, and he went to class supporting his sick body.

In the classroom, he sat on the prepared chair, talked about the book, but couldn't hold on until the end of the class. He wiped the sweat that was flowing down with a handkerchief! Even though it was winter, it flowed very heavily. He announced the end of the class.

Labor after the illness made his illness return to its original state, seemingly even worse.

Now, he was better again. But he was like a person who had lost consciousness, reading books at home every day, and guiding his children with their homework. That child also liked painting like him. He once said that he must work hard like Mr. Ziming in the future. Mr. Ziming only smiled bitterly at the child's words, and said in a dying low voice:

——Don't learn from me, I am useless.

Talking, he put down the tattered book, like he had regained the spirit of his youth, and corrected the child's painting.

Movie News

Silver Jottings 188

— Zhi Er

The Guarantee of Actors (Part 1)

I recently interviewed Miss Xia Peizhen. In addition to discussions on other aspects, she recounted some of the hardships she suffered when filming in the past. For example, when filming "Blood Debt", she said that she was thrown straight down from a mechanism more than ten feet high and fainted from the fall. Also, when filming "Daughter's Sutra", in the frigid winter morning, she was repeatedly blasted by a dozen water spouts, so much so that she couldn't cry or laugh. (She was supposed to be laughing in the play.)

And recently, in the Yihua Company's filming of "Father and Son Heroes", an actor named Wang Zhongkang also fell from a high set more than ten feet high, and could not move. It is said that he will have to stay in the hospital for three months.

When filming, in order to achieve realism, an actor needs to absolutely obey the director. Falling from a high place or being drenched in cold water, one time is not enough, followed by two or three times, or even four or five times, that is to be expected. However, in addition to being serious, after a shot is completed, or before a reshoot, the actor's body should be very carefully protected, which is also necessary. For example, after an actor is drenched in cold water, he should immediately be given a glass of brandy or something else to ward off the cold, so that he does not get sick. Also, for example, when filming a scene of falling from a high place (even if the play does not require a fall, but in order to prevent a misstep), there should also be equipment underneath to prevent falls and injuries, so as to avoid accidental damage to the actor. In addition to these necessary equipment, there should be a regular medical advisor to examine the actor's body, which is not an excessive request. This is not only a matter of "locking the fold after the sheep is stolen," but also a matter of "preventing problems before they happen." As for all the necessary medical expenses, they should naturally be borne by the company authorities, which is of course a matter of great justice.

Warner Bros.' Amazing Contribution "Human Hell" to be Publicly Performed Soon 189

The film industry giant Warner Bros. Pictures is famous for its tense, terrifying and stimulating productions. Since the giant film "Desperate" was released, it has become a sensation and won enthusiastic praise from all walks of life, breaking all box office records, and is the company's most honorable masterpiece. Warner Bros., in view of the need for such films, produced this "Desperate", even more exciting and tenser "Human Hell". The film stars the big star Donald Huazhi and the actress Katherine Knack, as well as the entire cast of the famous film "Iron-Blooded General", directed by the famous director Luo Yiqi and Jin. The entire film depicts a promising young man who, because he does not follow the instructions of politicians, is tricked into prison with his friend and suffers all kinds of hardships, whipping and torture. His friend could not bear it and wanted to escape, but was electrocuted by the electric fence. It was extremely tragic. Later, he angered the prison guards and was punished to work in a dark mine, which was even more painful. Later, he contacted various criminal miners, rebelled against the prison, and fought a major battle with the police. Finally, the young man gained his freedom and married his girlfriend. This film has a very touching depiction of the inhuman lives of criminals, and the cruel prison guards, etc., who grit their teeth and wish they could swallow them in one bite. In short, it is an extraordinary production. It is said that it will be publicly performed in the most noble theater in this city soon.

A Scene from "Girlfriend" 190

Shanghai Grand Theater screening

Performance News of the China Traveling Troupe 191

Starting from the 29th at the Carlton Theater. The plays include Camille, Thunderstorm, Mei Luoxiang.

Mr. Tang Huaiqiu, who leads the China Traveling Troupe, arrived in Shanghai on the 15th with a large number of scenery, costumes, props, etc., and is now staying at No. 13, Yingcun, Lafayette Road. It has been decided to start performing at the Carlton Theater on the 29th of this month. The first batch of plays are "Camille-Thunderstorm" and "Mei Yunxiang". Ticket prices are set at 50 cents, 70 cents, and one dollar. It is also scheduled to hold a preview performance at 9:30 AM on Sunday, the 26th, to entertain the press. The play for the preview may be "Camille".
